Skirting the southeast edge of Paris, this neighborhood claims Europe’s largest Chinatown—bringing with it traditionally delectable Asian cuisine and delightfully crowded streets. Beyond the pagodas that dot its landscape, high-rise towers, brick townhouses, and famous Basque restaurants share Place d’Italie – Quartier Chinois’ skyline."&gt;</span></p>

      <td valign="middle" class="td2">
        <p class="p2"><span class="s1">&lt;p class="lede"&gt;Place d’Italie – Quartier Chinois mixes business with pleasure. Skirting the southeast edge of Paris, this neighborhood claims Europe’s largest Chinatown—bringing with it traditionally delectable Asian cuisine and delightfully crowded streets. Beyond the pagodas that dot its landscape, high-rise towers, brick townhouses, and famous Basque restaurants share Place d’Italie – Quartier Chinois’ skyline.&lt;/p&gt;</span></p>
